They killed off the ocean where they built this ğŸ˜« Environmental Impacts The construction of the Palm Islands and The World, for all Nakheel's attempts to do otherwise, have had a clear and significant impact on the surrounding environment. It would be impossible to introduce a change of such magnitude to an established ecosystem and not anticipate any negative changes or reactions in the area's wildlife and natural processes. The construction of the various islands off the coast of Dubai has resulted in changes in area wildlife, coastal erosion and alongshore sediment transport, and wave patterns. Sediment stirred up by construction has suffocated and injured local marine fauna and reduced the amount of sunlight filtered down to seashore vegetation. Variations in alongshore sediment transport have resulted in changes in erosion patterns along the UAE coast, which has also been exacerbated by altered wave patterns as the waters of the Gulf attempt to move around the new obstruction of the islands.

I have a couple of questions.  1) How are they dealing with bio waste (I mean not food, but specifically poop and pee) on those islands without a sewage system and without it being transported away? Those islands are made out of sand, so I doubt you would just bury it on the islands. The "system" / bio factory he mentioned that converts food waste to methane gas doesn't work for poop and pee, does it.  2) Internet/tele comunication services. Those islands are in the middle of nowhere. How do they get Highspeed Internet over there? It surely is not Satellite. That would be way too expensive and inefficient. They must have lain a line underwater from mainland Dubai I assume? I would assume the same thing for electricity - a line being lain from mainland Dubai, but for electricity it's probably less of a problem, since they most definitely have solar power on those islands, and it will be enough to power the few people that will be living there. But for Internet it's different. I don't see how else you would get Highspeed Internet on those islands other than from having a cable lain from the mainland. I'm really curious about this in particular. Nobody who's planning to go to those islands, either to live or to rent, would want to be isolated without access to the Internet.   3) The chairman mentioned "desalination of sea water" (we desalinate, he said) as the way they are getting drinking water on those islands. I read up on that technology a bit to know it's advantages and disadvantages, and I wish the chairman would have elaborated more on the technology they use there. Are they using the thermal method - solar power to heat up and collect water vapor from sea water -  or are they using the membrane method - push sea water through a series of filters to pull out salt, other contaminants, and small sea life - or are the using both? What filters are they using? How modern/advanced? How big is the ecological footprint? How recent is the technology they are using there? In both of those desalination methods "brine" (that things that are filtered / remains) are all pumped back into the sea after all. It's a useful technology for sure, I just wish the chairman would have elaborated on how advanced the system is that they in particular are using. Is it advanced? Did they have a breakthrough in the filter system possibly? Are they using both systems? Or perhaps...are they still using the same desalination technology from the 1980s...?  Those were the things that came to my mind when I watched this video. A hypothetical situation, if I were to live on those islands longterm: Highspeed Internet? Freshwater? Sewage?
